 Policy 1312.3: Uniform Complaint Procedures                                                            ADOPTED
 Original Adopted Date: 09/08/1992 | Last Revised Date: 10/27/2020 | Last Reviewed Date: 10/27/2020

The governing board recognizes that the district has the primary responsibility to ensure compliance with
applicable state and federal laws and regula’┐Įons governing educa’┐Įonal programs. The board encourages
the early resolu’┐Įon of complaints whenever possible. To resolve complaints which may require a more
formal process, the board adopts the uniform system of complaint processes speci’¼üed in 5 CCR 4600-
4670, and the accompanying administra’┐Įve regula’┐Įon.

Complaints Subject to UCP
The district's uniform complaint procedures ("UCP") shall be used to inves’┐Įgate and resolve complaints
regarding the following programs and activities:the following complaints:

   1. Accommodations for pregnant and parenting students (Education Code 46015)

   2. Adult education programs (Education Code 8500-8538, 52334.7, 52500-52617)

   3. After School Education and Safety programs (Education Code 8482-8484.65)

   4. Agricultural career technical education (Education Code 52460-52462)

   5. Career technical and technical education and career technical and technical training
      programs (Education Code 52300-52462)

   6. Child care and development programs (Education Code 8200-8488)

   7. Compensatory education (Education Code 54400)

   8. Consolidated categorical aid programs (Education Code 33315; 34 CFR 299.10-299.12)

   9. Course periods without educational content (Education Code 51228.1-51228.3)

   10. Discrimination, harassment, intimidation, or bullying in district programs and activities, including
       in those programs or activities funded directly by or that receive or bene’¼üt from any state
       ’¼ünancial assistance, based on a person's actual or perceived characteristics of race or ethnicity,
       color, ancestry, nationality, national origin, immigration status, ethnic group identi’¼ücation, age,
       religion, marital status, pregnancy, parental status, physical or mental disability, medical condition,
       sex, sexual orientation, gender, gender identity, gender expression, or genetic information, or any
       other characteristic identi’¼üed in Education Code 200 or 220, Government Code 11135, or Penal
       Code 422.55, or based on the person's association with a person or group with one or more of
       these actual or perceived characteristics (5 CCR 4610)

        Discrimination includes, but is not limited to, the board's refusal to approve the use or prohibit
        the use of any textbook, instructional material, supplemental instructional material, or other
        curriculum for classroom instruction, or any book or other resource in a school library, on the
        basis that it includes a study of the role and contributions of any individual or group consistent
        with the requirements of Education Code 51204.5 and 60040, unless such study would violate
        Education Code 51501 or 60044. A complaint alleging such unlawful discrimination may, in
        addition to or in lieu of being ’¼üled with the district, be directly ’¼üled with the Superintendent of
        Public Instruction (ŌĆ£SPIŌĆØ). (Education Code 243)



                                                                                                                         1
 11. Educational and graduation requirements for students in foster care, students experiencing
     homelessness, students from military families, students formerly in a juvenile court school,
     students who are migratory, and students participating in a newcomer program (Education Code
     48645.7, 48853, 48853.5, 49069.5, 51225.1, 51225.2)

 12. Every Student Succeeds Act (Education Code 52059.5; 20 USC 6301 et seq.)

 13. Local control and accountability plan (Education Code 52075)

 14. Migrant education (Education Code 54440-54445

 15. Physical education instructional minutes (Education Code 51210, 51222, 51223)

 16. Student fees (Education Code 49010-49013)

 17. Reasonable accommodations to a lactating student (Education Code 222)

 18. Regional occupational centers and programs (Education Code 52300-52334.7)

 19. School plans for student achievement as required for the consolidated application for speci’¼üed
     federal and/or state categorical funding (Education Code 64001)

 20. School site councils as required for the consolidated application for speci’¼üed federal and/or state
     categorical funding (Education Code 65000)

 21. State preschool programs (Education Code 8207-8225)

 22. State preschool health and safety issues in license-exempt programs (Education Code 8212)

 23. Any complaint alleging retaliation against a complainant or other participant in the complaint
     process or anyone who has acted to uncover or report a violation subject to this policy

 24. Any other state or federal educational program the SPI or designee deems appropriate

   harassment, in’┐Įmida’┐Įon, or bullying) against any person in district programs and ac’┐Įvi’┐Įes
   including, but not limited to, those programs or ac’┐Įvi’┐Įes funded directly by or that receive or
   bene’¼üt from any state ’¼ünancial assistance, based on the person's actual or perceived

3. Any complaint alleging district noncompliance with the requirement to provide reasonable
   accommoda’┐Įon to a lacta’┐Įng student on school campuses to express breast milk, breas’┐Įeed an
   infant child, or address other breas’┐Įeeding-related needs of the student (Educa’┐Įon Code sec’┐Įon
   222).

4. Any complaint alleging district noncompliance with the requirements to provide a pregnant or
   paren’┐Įng student the accommoda’┐Įons speci’¼üed in Educa’┐Įon Code sec’┐Įon 46015, including those
   related to the provision of parental leave, right of return to the school of previous enrollment or to
   an alterna’┐Įve educa’┐Įon program, if desired, and possible enrollment in school for a ’¼ü’┐Įh year of
   instruc’┐Įon to enable the student to complete state and board-imposed gradua’┐Įon requirements
   (Educa’┐Įon Code sec’┐Įon 46015).

5. Any complaint alleging district noncompliance with the prohibi’┐Įon against requiring students to
   pay fees, deposits, or other charges for par’┐Įcipa’┐Įon in educa’┐Įonal ac’┐Įvi’┐Įes (5 CCR 4610).

6. Any complaint alleging district noncompliance with applicable requirements of Educa’┐Įon Code
   sec’┐Įons 52060-52077 related to the implementa’┐Įon of the local control and accountability plan
   ("LCAP"), including the development of a local control funding formula budget overview for
   parents/guardians (Educa’┐Įon Code
  sec’┐Įon 52075).

7. Any complaint alleging noncompliance with requirements related to the development of a school
   plan for student achievement or the establishment of a school site council, as required for the
   consolidated applica’┐Įon for speci’¼üed federal and/or state categorical funding (Educa’┐Įon Code
   sec’┐Įons 64000-64001, 65000-65001).

8. Any complaint, by or on behalf of any student who is a foster youth as de’¼üned in Educa’┐Įon Code
   sec’┐Įon 51225.2, alleging district noncompliance with any legal requirement applicable to the
   student regarding placement decisions; the responsibili’┐Įes of the district's educa’┐Įonal liaison to
   the student; the award of credit for coursework sa’┐Įsfactorily completed in another school, district,
   or country; school or records transfer; or the grant of an exemp’┐Įon from board-imposed
   gradua’┐Įon requirements (Educa’┐Įon Code sec’┐Įons 48853, 48853.5, 49069.5, 51225.1, and
   51225.2).

9. Any complaint, by or on behalf of a student who transfers into the district a’┐Įer the second year of
   high school and is a homeless child or youth as de’¼üned in 42 USC 11434a, a former juvenile court
   school student currently enrolled in the district, a child of a military family as de’¼üned in Educa’┐Įon
   Code sec’┐Įon 49701, a migrant student as de’¼üned in Educa’┐Įon Code sec’┐Įon 54441, or an
   immigrant student par’┐Įcipa’┐Įng in a newcomer program as de’¼üned in Educa’┐Įon Code sec’┐Įon
   51225.2 in the third or fourth year of high school, alleging district noncompliance with any
   requirement applicable to the student regarding the award of credit for coursework sa’┐Įsfactorily


                                                                                                            3
      completed in another school or district or the grant of an exemp’┐Įon from boardimposed
      gradua’┐Įon requirements (Educa’┐Įon Code sec’┐Įons 51225.1, 51225.2).

  10. Any complaint, by or on behalf of a student who is a homeless child or youth as de’¼üned in 42 USC
      11434a, a former juvenile court school student, a child of a military family as de’¼üned in Educa’┐Įon
      Code sec’┐Įon 49701, a migrant child as de’¼üned in Educa’┐Įon Code sec’┐Įon 54441, or a newly arrived
      immigrant student who is par’┐Įcipa’┐Įng in a newcomer program as de’¼üned in Educa’┐Įon Code
      sec’┐Įon 51225.2, alleging district noncompliance with requirements for the award of credit for
      coursework sa’┐Įsfactorily completed in another school, district, or country (Educa’┐Įon Code sec’┐Įon
      51225.2)

  11. Any complaint alleging district noncompliance with the requirements of Educa’┐Įon Code sec’┐Įons
      51228.1 and 51228.2 that prohibit the assignment of a student in grades 9-12 to a course without
      educa’┐Įonal content for more than one week in any semester or to a course the student has
      previously sa’┐Įsfactorily completed, without mee’┐Įng speci’¼üed condi’┐Įons (Educa’┐Įon Code sec’┐Įon
      51228.3).

  12. Any complaint alleging district noncompliance with the physical educa’┐Įon instruc’┐Įonal minutes
      requirement for students in elementary school (Educa’┐Įon Code sec’┐Įons 51210, 51222, 51223).

  13. Complaints regarding the noncompliance of a license-exempt California State Preschool Program
      (CSPP) with health and safety standards speci’¼üed in Health and Safety Code sec’┐Įon 1596.7925 and
      related state regula’┐Įons (Educa’┐Įon Code sec’┐Įon 8235.5; Health and Safety Code sec’┐Įon
      1596.7925)

  14. Any complaint alleging retalia’┐Įon against a complainant or other par’┐Įcipant in the complaint
      process or anyone who has acted to uncover or report a viola’┐Įon subject to this policy.

  15. Any other complaint as speci’¼üed in a district policy.
The board recognizes that alterna’┐Įve dispute resolu’┐Įon ("ADR") can, depending on the nature of the
allega’┐Įons, o’¼Ćer a process to reach a resolu’┐Įon to thefor resolving a complaint in a manner that is
acceptable to all par’┐Įes. An ADR process such as media’┐Įon may be o’¼Ćered to resolve complaints that
involve more than one student and no adult. However, media’┐Įon shall not be o’¼Ćered or used to resolve any
complaint involving sexual assault or where there is a reasonable risk that a party to the media’┐Įon would
feel compelled to par’┐Įcipate. The superintendent or designee shall ensure that the use of ADR is consistent
with state and federal laws and regula’┐Įons.
The district shall protect all complainants from retalia’┐Įon. In inves’┐Įga’┐Įng complaints, the con’¼üden’┐Įality
of the par’┐Įes involved shall be protected as required by law. For any complaint alleging retalia’┐Įon or
unlawful discrimina’┐Įon (such as discriminatory harassment, in’┐Įmida’┐Įon, or bullying), the superintendent
or designee shall keep the iden’┐Įty of the complainant and/or the subject of the complaint, if he/she is
di’¼Ćerent from the complainant, and/or the subject of the complaint if di’¼Ćerent from the complainant,
con’¼üden’┐Įal when appropriate and as long as the integrity of the complaint process is maintained.
When an allega’┐Įon that is not subject to the UCP is included in a UCP complaint, the district shall refer the
non-UCP allega’┐Įon to the appropriate sta’¼Ć or agency and shall inves’┐Įgate and, if appropriate, resolve the
UCP-related allega’┐Įon(s) through the district's UCP process.
The superintendent or designee shall provide training to district sta’¼Ć to ensure awareness and knowledge
of current law and related requirements related to UCP, including the steps and ’┐Įmelines speci’¼üed in this
policy and the accompanying administra’┐Įve regula’┐Įon.
The superintendent or designee shall maintain a record of each complaint and subsequent related ac’┐Įons,
including steps taken during the inves’┐Įga’┐Įon and all informa’┐Įon required for compliance with 5 CCR 4631
and 4633.

Non-UCP Complaints

                                                                                                              4
The following complaints shall not be subject to the district's UCP but shall be investigated and
resolved by the speci’¼üed agency or through an alternative process: The following complaints shall not
be subject to the district's UCP but shall be referred to the speci’¼üed agency: (5 CCR 4611)
   1. Any complaint alleging child abuse or neglect shall be referred to the County Department of Social
      Services Protec’┐Įve Services Division and or the appropriate law enforcement agency. (5 CCR 4611)

   2. Any complaint alleging health and safety viola’┐Įons by a child development program shall, for
      licensed facili’┐Įes, be referred to Department of Social Services and shall, for licensing-exempt
      facili’┐Įes, be referred to the appropriate Child Development regional administrator. (5 CCR 4611)


   2.3. Any complaint alleging that a student, while in an education program or activity in which the
      district exercises substantial control over the context and respondent, was subjected to sexual
      harassment as de’¼üned in 34 CFR 106.30 shall be addressed through the federal Title IX complaint
      procedures adopted pursuant to 34 CFR 106.44-106.45, as speci’¼üed in Administrative Regulation
      5145.71 - Title IX Sexual Harassment Complaint Procedures.

   4. Any complaint alleging employment discrimina’┐Įon or harassment shall be inves’┐Įgated and resolved
      by the district in accordance with the procedures speci’¼üed in Administra’┐Įve Regula’┐Įon 4030 -
      Nondiscrimina’┐Įon in Employment, including the right to ’¼üle the complaint with the California Civil
      Rights Department of Fair Employment and Housing.


   3.5. Any complaint alleging a violation of a state or federal law or regulation related to special
      education, a settlement agreement related to the provision of a free appropriate public education
      (FAPE), failure or refusal to implement a due process hearing order to which the district is subject,
      or a physical safety concern that interferes with the district's provision of FAPE shall be submitted
      to the California Department of Education (CDE) in accordance with Administrative Regulation
      6159.1 - Procedural Safeguards and Complaints for Special Education. (5 CCR 3200-3205)

   4. 6. Any complaint alleging noncompliance of the district's food service program with laws
      regarding meal counting and claiming, reimbursable meals, eligibility of children or adults, or use
      of cafeteria funds and allowable expenses shall be ’¼üled with or referred to CDE in accordance
      with Board Policy 3555 - Nutrition Program Compliance. (5 CCR 15580-15584)Any complaint
      alleging fraud shall be referred to the Legal, Audits and Compliance Branch of the California
      Department of Educa’┐Įon.
7. Any allegation of discrimination based on race, color, national origin, sex, age, or disability in the
district's food service program shall be ’¼üled with or referred to the U.S. Department of Agriculture in
accordance with Board Policy 3555 - Nutrition Program Compliance. (5 CCR 15582)
8. Any complaint related to su’¼āciency of textbooks or instruc’┐Įonal materials, emergency or urgent
facili’┐Įes condi’┐Įons that pose a threat to the health or safety of students or sta’¼Ć, or teacher vacancies and
misassignments shall be inves’┐Įgated and resolved in accordance with the procedures in AR Administra’┐Įve
Regula’┐Įon 1312.4 - Williams Uniform Complaint Procedures. (Educa’┐Įon Code sec’┐Įon 8235.5, 35186)

ACTION REQUESTED:
The superintendent is recommending that the board discuss the proposed revisions to Board Policy
5145.3 Nondiscrimination/Harassment.

Action Anticipated: 01/23/2024

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
The revisions are suggested because California School Boards Association (CSBA) has updated the language
for Board Policy 5145.3 Nondiscrimination/Harassment. In order to align the districtŌĆÖs policy with CSBA,
revisions are being suggested.


ATTACHMENT(S):
A: Proposed revisions to Board Policy 5145.3 Nondiscrimination/Harassment



BOARD COMMITTEE ACTION/COMMENT:
N/A

SuperintendentŌĆÖs Cabinet: 12/18/2023

                                                                                                                  Attachment A
                                                                                                 Board Policy Manual
                                                                                       San Juan Uni’¼üed School District
                                                                                              Printed: 11/13/2023 04:05 PM

                                                                                                        Status:
 Policy 5145.3: Nondiscrimina’┐Įon/Harassment                                                             ADOPTED
 Original Adopted Date: 04/28/2015 | Last Revised Date: 04/25/2023 | Last Reviewed Date: 04/25/2023

This policy shall apply to all acts constituting unlawful discrimination or harassment related to
school activity or to school attendance occurring within a district school, to acts which occur o’¼Ć
campus or outside of school-related or school-sponsored activities but which may have an impact
or create a hostile environment at school, and to all acts of the Governing Board and the
superintendent in enacting policies and procedures that govern the district.
The governing board desires to provide a welcoming, safe, and suppor’┐Įve school environment that allows
all students equal access and opportuni’┐Įes in the district's academic, extracurricular, and other
educa’┐Įonal support programs, services, and ac’┐Įvi’┐Įes. The board prohibits, at any district school or
school ac’┐Įvity, unlawful discrimina’┐Įon, including discriminatory harassment (including sexual
harassment), in’┐Įmida’┐Įon, and bullying targeted at any student by anyone, based on the student's actual
or perceived race, color, ancestry, na’┐Įonal origin, na’┐Įonality, immigra’┐Įon status, ethnicity, ethnic group
iden’┐Į’¼üca’┐Įon, age, religion, marital or parental status, pregnancy, physical or mental disability, medical
condi’┐Įon, sex, sexual orienta’┐Įon, gender, gender iden’┐Įty, gender expression, gene’┐Įc informa’┐Įon, or
a’¼ālia’┐Įon with the Boys Scouts of America, or associa’┐Įon with a person or group with one or more of
these actual or perceived characteris’┐Įcs.

This policy shall apply to all acts related to school ac’┐Įvity or to school atendance occurring within a
district school. (Educa’┐Įon Code sec’┐Įon 234.1) This policy shall also apply to acts which occur o’¼Ć campus
or outside of schoolrelated or school-sponsored ac’┐Įvi’┐Įes but which may have an impact or create a
hos’┐Įle environment at school.

Unlawful discrimina’┐Įon, including discriminatory harassment (including sexual harassment), in’┐Įmida’┐Įon,
or bullying or the crea’┐Įon of a hos’┐Įle environment, may result from physical, verbal, nonverbal, or writen
conduct based on any of the categories listed above. Unlawful discrimina’┐Įon also includes the crea’┐Įon of
a hos’┐Įle environment throughoccurs when prohibited conduct that is so severe, persistent, or pervasive
that it a’¼Ćects a student's ability to par’┐Įcipate in or bene’¼üt from an educa’┐Įonal program or ac’┐Įvity;
creates an in’┐Įmida’┐Įng, threatening, hos’┐Įle, or o’¼Ćensive educa’┐Įonal environment; has the e’¼Ćect of
substan’┐Įally or unreasonably interfering with a student's academic performance; or otherwise adversely
a’¼Ćects a student's educa’┐Įonal opportuni’┐Įes.

Unlawful discrimina’┐Įon also includes disparate treatment of students based on one of the above
iden’┐Į’¼üed categories above with respect to the provision of opportuni’┐Įes to par’┐Įcipate in school
programs or ac’┐Įvi’┐Įes or the provision or receipt of educa’┐Įonal bene’¼üts or services.

Because unlawful discrimination may occur when disciplining students, including suspension and
expulsion, the superintendent or designee shall ensure that sta’¼Ć enforce discipline rules fairly,
consistently and in a non-discriminatory manner, as speci’¼üed in Board Policy and Administrative
Regulation 5144 - Discipline, Board Policy and Administrative Regulation 5144.1 - Suspension and
Expulsion/Due Process, and Administrative Regulation 5144.2 - Suspension and Expulsion/Due
Process (Students With Disabilities).
The board also prohibits any form of retalia’┐Įon against any individual who ’¼üles, reports or par’┐Įcipates in
the repor’┐Įng of unlawful discrimina’┐Įon, ’¼üles or, or otherwise par’┐Įcipates in the ’¼üling of a complaint, or
inves’┐Įgates or par’┐Įcipates in the, repor’┐Įng, or inves’┐Įga’┐Įon of a complaint or report alleging unlawful

                                                                                                                         1
discrimina’┐Įon, including discriminatory harassment, in’┐Įmida’┐Įon, or bullying. Retalia’┐Įon complaints shall
be inves’┐Įgated and resolved in the same manner as a discrimina’┐Įon complaint.

The superintendent or designee shall facilitate students' access to the educa’┐Įonal program by publicizing
the district's nondiscrimina’┐Įon policy and related complaint procedures to students, parents/guardians,
and employees. In addition, the superintendent or designee shall post the district's policies
prohibiting discrimination, harassment, intimidation, and bullying and other required information
on the district's website in a manner that is easily accessible to parents/guardians and students, in
accordance with law and the accompanying administrative regulation. (Education Code sections
234.1, 234.6)
The superintendent or designee shall provide training and/or informa’┐Įon on the scope and use of the
policy and complaint procedures and take other measures designed to increase the school community's
understanding of the requirements of law related to discrimina’┐Įon. The superintendent or designee shall
regularly review the implementa’┐Įon of the district's nondiscrimina’┐Įon policies and prac’┐Įces and, as
necessary, shall take ac’┐Įon to remove any iden’┐Į’¼üed barrier to student access to or par’┐Įcipa’┐Įon in the
districtŌĆÖs educa’┐Įonal program. The superintendent or designee shall report their ’¼ündings and
recommenda’┐Įons to the board a’┐Įer each review.

Regardless of whether a complainant complies with the wri’┐Įng, ’┐Įmeline, and/or other formal ’¼üling
requirements, all complaints alleging unlawful discrimina’┐Įon, including discriminatory harassment
(including sexual harassment), in’┐Įmida’┐Įon, or bullying, shall be inves’┐Įgated and prompt ac’┐Įon taken to
stop the discrimina’┐Įon, prevent recurrence, and address any con’┐Įnuing e’¼Ćect on students.

Students who engage in unlawful discrimina’┐Įon, including discriminatory harassment (including sexual
harassment), in’┐Įmida’┐Įon, bullying, or retalia’┐Įon, in viola’┐Įon of law, board policy, or administra’┐Įve
regula’┐Įon shall be subject to appropriate consequence or discipline, which may include suspension or
expulsion when the behavior is severe or pervasive as de’¼üned in Educa’┐Įon Code sec’┐Įon 48900.4. Any
employee who permits or engages in prohibited discrimina’┐Įon, including discriminatory harassment
(including sexual harassment), in’┐Įmida’┐Įon, bullying, or retalia’┐Įon shall be subject to disciplinary ac’┐Įon,
up to and including dismissal.

All allegations of unlawful discrimination in district programs and activities shall be brought,
investigated, and resolved in accordance with Board Policy 1312.3 - Uniform Complaint
Procedures.
The district designates the individuals iden’┐Į’¼üed below as the employees responsible for coordina’┐Įng the
district's e’¼Ćorts to comply with applicable state and federal civil rights laws, including Title IX of the
Educa’┐Įon Amendments of 1972, Sec’┐Įon 504 of the Rehabilita’┐Įon Act of 1973, Title II of the Americans
with Disabili’┐Įes Act, and the Age
Discrimina’┐Įon Act of 1975, and to answer inquiries regarding the district's nondiscrimina’┐Įon policies. The
individual(s) shall also serve as the compliance o’¼ācer(s) speci’¼üed in AR 1312.3 - Uniform Complaint
Procedures as the responsible employee to handle complaints alleging unlawful discrimina’┐Įon targe’┐Įng a
student, including discriminatory harassment (including sexual harassment), in’┐Įmida’┐Įon, or bullying,
based on the student's actual or perceived race, color, ancestry, na’┐Įonality, na’┐Įonal origin, na’┐Įonality,
immigra’┐Įon status, ethnicity, ethnic group iden’┐Į’¼üca’┐Įon, ethnicity, age, religion, marital status, parental
status, pregnancy, physical or mental disability, sex, sexual orienta’┐Įon, gender, gender iden’┐Įty, gender
expression, gene’┐Įc informa’┐Įon, or any other legally protected status or associa’┐Įon with a person or
group with one or more of these actual or perceived characteris’┐Įcs. (Educa’┐Įon Code sec’┐Įon 234.1; 5 CCR
4621)

Process for Ini’┐Įa’┐Įng and Responding to Complaints

The general counsel or designee may assign other sta’¼Ć to inves’┐Įgate based on the nature of the complaint
as directed under BP/AR 1312.3, Uniform Complaint Procedures.

Any student who feels that they have been subjected to unlawful discrimina’┐Įon, including discriminatory
harassment (including sexual harassment), in’┐Įmida’┐Įon, or bullying is strongly encouraged to immediately
contact the general counsel, the principal, or any other district employee. Any student who observes any
such incident is strongly encouraged to report the incident to the general counsel or principal, or any
other district employee whether or not the vic’┐Įm ’¼üles a complaint. Any district employee who observes
an incident of unlawful discrimina’┐Įon, including discriminatory harassment (including sexual harassment),
in’┐Įmida’┐Įon, or bullying shall report the incident to their supervisor, the general counsel, or principal,
whether or not the vic’┐Įm ’¼üles a complaint. In addi’┐Įon, the district employee shall immediately intervene
when safe to do so. (Educa’┐Įon Code sec’┐Įon 234.1)

Upon receiving a complaint of unlawful discrimina’┐Įon, including discriminatory harassment (including
sexual harassment), in’┐Įmida’┐Įon, or bullying, the general counsel or designee shall immediately
inves’┐Įgate the complaint in accordance with AR 1312.3, Uniform Complaint Procedures.

The general counsel shall ensure that the student and parent handbook clearly describes the district's
nondiscrimina’┐Įon policy, procedures for ’¼üling a complaint regarding unlawful discrimina’┐Įon, including
discriminatory harassment (including sexual harassment), in’┐Įmida’┐Įon, or bullying, and the resources that
may be available to students who feel that they have been the vic’┐Įm of any such behavior. The district's
policy shall also be posted on the district web site or any other loca’┐Įon that is easily accessible to
students.

Record-Keeping

                                                                                                            3
The superintendent or designee shall maintain a record of all reported cases of unlawful discrimina’┐Įon,
including discriminatory harassment, in’┐Įmida’┐Įon, or bullying, to enable the district to monitor, address,
and prevent repe’┐Į’┐Įve prohibited behavior in district schools.

                                                                         Emergency Action:



ACTION REQUESTED:
The superintendent is recommending the board receive a report regarding Williams-type complaints filed with
the district during the time period from October 1, 2023, to December 31, 2023.


RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
The Williams legislation embodied in Education Code section 35186(d) requires each school district to publicly
report, on a quarterly basis, summarized data on the nature and resolution of all Williams-type complaints filed
with the district.


ATTACHMENT(S):
A: Williams Act 2nd Quarterly Report


BOARD COMMITTEE ACTION/COMMENT:
N/A
